Datathletics Neural Network

Objectives

  • Find the stability of the network: given the sparce representation of the population, will there be a substantial structural difference when looking at the model for a 5-year age span versus a 15-year age span? Or will the outputs be relatively smooth?

  • Rerun different networks with the same inputs and determine a comparison of the outputs from each other

  • Reconsider the architecture of the network

  • Create a more constrained analysis by generalizing the network: use 3 adjacent 5-year age-spans (therefore 45 outputs) and backpropagate through the network to find the differences in the hidden layers -- still not sure if I have a full understanding of this?

How well are we converting to an outcome? What is the natural variability and the consistency of our results??

# from race_bins.py

BIN_SIZE = 15 #

def get_bins(race_data):
    """ Group races and create bins (time ranges) of BIN_SIZE. For each
        bin find out pct of racers in that bin and avg time of that bin.
        Also assign bin number to identify racers and their bin they fall
        into later on.
    """
    bin_data = []
    race_groups = race_data.groupby('race_id')

    for race_id, race_group in race_groups:

        # Subset to look at specifically the top 75% because the bottom quantile's data is a bit messier  
        top_75_percentile = race_group[
            race_group.final_time < race_group.final_time.quantile(.75)]

        # Skip races with missing data.
        if len(top_75_percentile) == 0:
            continue

        bins = pd.cut(top_75_percentile.final_time, BIN_SIZE, right=False)

        # fastest = time.strftime(
        #     '%H:%M:%S', time.gmtime(min(top_75_percentile.final_time)))
        # slowest = time.strftime(
        #     '%H:%M:%S', time.gmtime(max(top_75_percentile.final_time)))

        # print "fastest =>", fastest
        # print "slowest =>", slowest

        bin_number = 0

        for bin_key, bin_group in top_75_percentile.groupby(bins):

            bin_number += 1

            population_pct = len(bin_group) / float(len(top_75_percentile))
            bin_avg_time = bin_group.final_time.mean()

            if math.isnan(bin_avg_time):
                # Yes Ugly. Pandas bin key is a string.
                # This split gives us bin's lower/upper range time.
                lower_range = float(first(bin_key.split(',')).strip('['))
                upper_range = float(last(bin_key.split(',')).strip(')'))

                bin_avg_time = np.mean([lower_range, upper_range])

            bin_data.append({'race_id': int(race_id),
                             'bin_number': bin_number,
                             'population_pct': population_pct,
                             'bin_avg_time': bin_avg_time
                             })
    return bin_data
In [3]: 
def _sum_square_error(actual, desired):
    error = 0.
    for i in range(len(desired)):
        for j in range(len(desired[i])):
            error = error + \
                ((actual[i])[j] - (desired[i])[j]) * (
                    (actual[i])[j] - (desired[i])[j])

    return error

Get Supervised Dataset

Input has 6 race conditions: high temp, low temp, high humidity, low humidity, starting elevation, and gross elevation gain

Output has the 15 population percentage bins

Neural network will learn based off the race conditions what the population percentage distribution will look like

In [12]: 
data_set = SupervisedDataSet(6, 15)

comparison_data_set = SupervisedDataSet(6,15)
In [13]: 
for race_id, race_bin in race_bin_groups:

    # Skip bins with fewer than 10% race population
    if not np.count_nonzero(race_bin.population_pct) > 10:
        continue
        
    race_factor = race_factors[race_factors.race_id == race_id] # subset by matching race id to race_factors to obtain conditions info

    # If race has missing factor data then skip
    if race_factor.empty:
        continue

    input_factors = [first(race_factor.high_temp) / 100.0,
                     first(race_factor.low_temp) / 100.0,
                     first(race_factor.high_humidity) / 100.0,
                     first(race_factor.low_humidity) / 100.0,            
                     first(race_factor.starting_elevation) / 10000.0,
                     first(race_factor.gross_elevation_gain) / 10000.0
                    ]

    output_factors = race_bin.population_pct.tolist()

    data_set.appendLinked(input_factors, output_factors)

for race_id, race_bin in race_comparison_bin_groups:

    # Skip bins with fewer than 10% race population
    if not np.count_nonzero(race_bin.population_pct) > 10:
        continue
        
    race_factor = race_factors[race_factors.race_id == race_id] # subset by matching race id to race_factors to obtain conditions info

    # If race has missing factor data then skip
    if race_factor.empty:
        continue

    input_factors = [first(race_factor.high_temp) / 100.0,
                     first(race_factor.low_temp) / 100.0,
                     first(race_factor.high_humidity) / 100.0,
                     first(race_factor.low_humidity) / 100.0,            
                     first(race_factor.starting_elevation) / 10000.0,
                     first(race_factor.gross_elevation_gain) / 10000.0
                    ]

    output_factors = race_bin.population_pct.tolist()

    comparison_data_set.appendLinked(input_factors, output_factors)

In [17]: 
supervised_dataset = data_set # in original code, goes through the actual function here 
trainData, testData = supervised_dataset.splitWithProportion(0.9)
  • Create 100 neural networks
  • Activate each network with random weights
  • Train each network with the same inputs from the 5-year age span
  • Continue training until the error between y and the predicted output of the network converges to 1E-3
In [19]: 
start = timeit.default_timer()

networks = []
trainers = []

for i in range(100): 
    networks += [buildNetwork(6, 5, 15)]
    networks[i].sortModules()
    networks[i].activate(numpy.random.uniform(-1, 1, size=6))
    trainers += [BackpropTrainer(networks[i], dataset = trainData)]
    temp = 1
    while True:
        trainers[i].trainEpochs(5)
        error = _sum_square_error(networks[i].activateOnDataset(dataset=trainData),  trainData['target'])
        print 'Network: ', i, 'Error: ', error
        if abs(temp - error) < 0.001:
            print 'Execution time =>', timeit.default_timer() - start, 'secs'
            break
        else:
            temp = error

take 100 networks of 22 arrays and find the average of each array for each index.

  1. compute outputs for each network on the same set of testing data
  2. collapse outputs into one array
  3. take average - axis = 0
  4. compare each individual network to the average and find the MSE of the outputs
In [172]: 
outputs = [] 

for i in range(len(networks)):
    outputs += [networks[i].activateOnDataset(dataset=testData)]
In [176]: 
collapsed_outputs = np.array(outputs)
averaged_outputs = np.mean(collapsed_outputs, axis=0) ## created one averaged array of length 22
In [209]: 
error = []
for i in range(100): 
    inderror = _sum_square_error(outputs[i], averaged_outputs)
    error += [inderror]
    print "Network: ", i, "Error: ", inderror

  • Create 100 neural networks
  • Activate each network with random weights
  • Train each network with the same inputs from the 15-year age span
  • Continue training until the error between y and the predicted output of the network converges to 1E-3
In [167]: 
start = timeit.default_timer()

networks_fifteen = []
trainers_fifteen = []

for i in range(100): 
    networks_fifteen += [buildNetwork(6, 5, 15)]
    networks_fifteen[i].sortModules()
    networks_fifteen[i].activate(numpy.random.uniform(-1, 1, size=6))
    trainers_fifteen += [BackpropTrainer(networks_fifteen[i], dataset = trainData_fifteen)]
    temp = 1
    while True:
        trainers_fifteen[i].trainEpochs(5)
        error = _sum_square_error(networks_fifteen[i].activateOnDataset(dataset=trainData_fifteen),  trainData_fifteen['target'])
        print 'Network: ', i, 'Error: ', error
        if abs(temp - error) < 0.001:
            print 'Execution time =>', timeit.default_timer() - start, 'secs'
            break
        else:
            temp = error

IGNORE BELOW - notes and practice outputs for personal use

In [113]: 
final_averaged_outputs = []

for j in range(22):
    for i in range(100):
        output = networks[i].activateOnDataset(dataset=testData)
        if i == 0: 
            to_average = output[j]
        else: 
            to_average = np.vstack((to_average, output[j]))
    if j == 0: 
        final_averaged_outputs = np.mean(to_average, axis=0)
    else:
        final_averaged_outputs = np.vstack((final_averaged_outputs, np.mean(to_average, axis=0)))
In []: 
final_averaged_outputs_fifteen = []

for j in range(len(networks_fifteen[0])):
    for i in range(len(networks_fifteen)):
        output = networks_fifteen[i].activateOnDataset(dataset=testData_fifteen)
        if i == 0: 
            to_average = output[j]
        else: 
            to_average = np.vstack((to_average, output[j]))
    if j == 0: 
        final_averaged_outputs_fifteen = np.mean(to_average, axis=0)
    else:
        final_averaged_outputs_fifteen = np.vstack((final_averaged_outputs_fifteen, np.mean(to_average, axis=0)))
